Re: Building the 8 Footer Star Destroyer Bridge and Neck

Right- a quick proposal:

Any further endeavors along the studio scale front must require a studio scale uniform, qualities of the uniform to be appropriate to the time period which you are representing in your work. For instance, given the time period of the construction of the model mentioned in this thread, a late '70s button down short sleeve (er, polo) shirt, is required.

For ANH and slightly thereafter era works, all men shall have beards, and at least one day per week shall wear cut-off jeans and basic t-shirts. At various points you are allowed long sleeve button down shirts and crew t-shirts. You can not stop at a moustache and a special no-no is a moustache and polo shirt combination (this was Paul Huston's thing... and he still does it)

Hair should always be appropriately styled, but remember that if you are going from a RotJ model to ANH, you have to allow for hair and beard length adjustments, so schedule appropriately.

Great project; I'm am, as others, certain that your final results will be solid indeed.

Re: Building the 8 Footer Star Destroyer Bridge and Neck

Thanks for your support and all of your comments guys !

Yeah Mike I (really) need a shave ! But Im not like Lorne though :lol

Unfortunatly 24 hours a day here too Guy ! Would love to get more though, I need to finish a lot of stuff ! 

Matt, you're right that's something which would be impossible with a resin kit (except if you cast each part !). With good lighting it should be really cool ! Of course I'll add FO.

Clerval, do you mean something like that : 

[IMAGE: bridge-tshirt.jpg]

? Since it was released for the crew working on TESB, probably someone did wear it while building the ISD :lol But I dont wear it when modeling, I'm not a geek ! Only when I am at work :lol

Max, Stu : The whole model would cost me an arm (and maybe my GF but at least a lot of money and space 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
). I would have space to build and display it but unfortunatly once built I couldnt move it from this room  I would have to build it in section to be able to go through the door...

Perhaps if each RPF member send me one kitpart, I would be able to fully detail the whole model ! 

Joke aside, the frame itself would cost a lot (I cant imagine 8 feet plexi plates !). I could build the superstructures though :

[IMAGE: ISDILMbuildingpic4.jpg]

But I cant lie and tell you that Ive never thought about the whole model !

Yes Stu it will be shame to put primer on it (even if I love the result after a coat of primer !) because of all the colored parts ! Once I got that I will be very happy !

[IMAGE: ISDILMbuildingpic5.jpg]

Omes I did rough plans of the bridge frame (front, sides top and bottom, not the back plates, I cut them larger and adapted to the other faces). I have to draw the neck now. It's quite hard because of all the angles, lenses distorsion etc... But fortunatly the kitparts used on the neck are quite big !

). And yes I plan to do the decks (perhaps more than the deck

Anyway thanks for your interest guys !

Post #31  (forum post #964113)
Author    : MonsieurTox
Date      : Aug 20, 2009 at 1:31 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8 Footer Star Destroyer Bridge and Neck

Hey guys, today I received my HMS Hood so I was able to glue most of the parts ! The Hood deck was really hard to cut (the plastic of my copy is very hard !).

 I also did the plating on the lower facia. It was quite hard because ILM add it after they glued all the parts, this means that you have to do cutouts on the styrene plates where the parts are. I noticed that the details on the right and on the left of the hood parts were not exactly at the same height on the ILM model. That's why they added a plate on the portside which creates a kind of step when you watch it. The leading edge of this plate not follow the lower facia angle, it's not parallel. That's quite weird, isnt it ? Well I did my best to recreate that (unfortunatly my parts were not misaligned like on the studio model so I add to move them quite a bit 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
).

Ok now here some pics with and without flash (those last ones are a bit blurry, sorry...)

[IMAGE: 8ft33.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft34.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft35.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft36.jpg]

Unfortunatly I noticed that my lang part is glued 0.5-1mm to low so it means all the parts under it are also 0.5-1mm too low. Well I can live with that...

I received my 2" finials. Unfortunatly 2" was the overall heignt, not the diameter of the finials :angry. I ordered this time 2" diameter finials (I asked before 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
), Im waiting for them ! Hopefully those ones will work...

Post #61  (forum post #969729)
Author    : MonsieurTox
Date      : Aug 27, 2009 at 2:02 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8 Footer Star Destroyer Bridge and Neck

Thanks guys,

Lasse I'm very glad and honored you posted here. Your work was and still is one of my first inspiration.

I've finished the plating of the back. Then I sprayed a light coat of primer. I dont say the plating is 100% accurate, but I did my best to recreate what "I think" is right. Probably some mistakes though... Although once primed it looks nice IMHO :

[IMAGE: 8ft46.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft47.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft48.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft49.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft50.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft51.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft52.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft53.jpg]

2 or 3 parts are missing. I havent ID'ed them yet. I'll add them later if I ever find them, if not I'll scratchbuilt them prior to paint the whole thing.

I removed the large armor plate on the starboard side and replace it with a new one. Yeah, because this part has some tiny raised details on the back and I sanded them on my first attempt. Then I noticed that they glued it with those raised details which creates a void between the bridge and the part (very noticiable from the front).

I got balls ! Yeah, crystal balls, this time they are just about the right size ! 

[IMAGE: 8ft54.jpg]

Since they are done by hand (OMG it's very heavy I dont know how I will secure them on the top of the bridge !), the faces are not evenly done. But it will not be very noticiable once I put all those triangular styrene chips on it.

Please let me know honest thought about the plating of the back ?

Thanks guys !

Reactions : Like — struschie
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

Hey guys,

Not huge updates (for you) but a huge work (for me).

The Karl and the ford engine parts well not at the right place. What a pain to remove them with care... Took me one hour.

[IMAGE: 8ft57.jpg]

Since the part was not usable I had to use another one. Unfortunatly in 2 of my Karl kits the parts are not well molded !

(on the left a good one)

[IMAGE: 8ft58.jpg]

See the flaws !

[IMAGE: 8ft59.jpg]

Well finally all is good :

[IMAGE: 8ft61.jpg]

The Karl and Gneisenau parts are not glued yet since I dont know what is the part behind them.

I removed the styrene strips on the top of the bridge because I saw on my new reference material that I was a bit off. It was the good time to exchange the Mobelwagen armor plates. Here again it was very hard to remove them without hurting the surrounding parts.

[IMAGE: 8ft60.jpg]

That's look OK, TBH I was not affected by those 2 parts but since I had the opportunity to change them, Im glad of the result even if its not very noticiable..

I found a part which is very similar to the right one : 

[IMAGE: 8ft64.jpg]

Not 100% correct but since we dont know the right one, this will do the job. Ill replace it if we ever find the correct one.

Allan (Imaginager) sent me the T34 parts, I cast it and put it in place : 

[IMAGE: 8ft63.jpg]

Thanks Allan !

Post #90  (forum post #975282)
Author    : MonsieurTox
Date      : Sep 3, 2009 at 3:24 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

Many thanks for your comments guys !

Stu, unfortunatly it would have been too easy with cyano :/ I used orange and green tamiya glue which literally melt and welt the plastic. That's a cold welding :/

Rob I think it would make sense. Sisterships I never the same in the real world so why not in the Star Wars universe ? Just take a look at the X-Wings, Y-Wings, AT-ST's... None of them are exactly the same !

Thanks Martyn, and thanks again for your help 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

SWGeek : Im wondering if I should go this way... That's a big problem for me because if I had the little trianular styrene plates, it would create a ton of sharp edges (sharper than the crystal edges). It means a lot of trap for airbubbles (I cant do pressure casting). But in the other hands, cut thousand of exactly the same parts would be time consuming. I dont know what to do ! I think I will try to do a mold with all the styrne plates in place and if it doesnt work, Ill cast the second and naked crystal !
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #106  (forum post #995712)
Author    : Dyonisis
Date      : Sep 28, 2009 at 1:08 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

omes72 said:

			Monsieur Tox. Who or what is 'CNC' for the plexi glass hull scribing? Very interested in not missing any detail. Cheers & fantastic work.
		

Click to expand...

 CNC = Computer Numerically Controlled router.  CNC for short. This is done by computing numbers geometrically to give an exact shape of a given subject.  This is written on a computer,then it is transferred to a readable file for the CNC machine,and programmed from that file to CNC permanently for a long run of parts,or until another project requires that CNC to be programmed with another subject file. This works somewhat like a disc drive on your computer. You insert the disc with a file,or the information you want it to have,and then download it. The computer deciphers the rest of the information,and encodes it,so that it will come out the same way in a 3-D form cut from wood,plastic,or metal.
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

I also have the plexi plate for the main hulls (need to be cut, but since it's straight cut I would be able to do it by myself). 

Unfortunatly some parts will be impossible to find because of the lack of reference of some areas. We can see there is a part but the pics is too fuzzy/far and it's impossible to ID so Ill have to do some artistic choice. 

Would love to finish it for 2010 (30th anniversary of TESB), it will be quite hard though ! My biggest concern is where to paint it and how I would be able to move it. I would have to rent a truck probably since I cant split the hull in half !

Post #140  (forum post #1033332)
Author    : MonsieurTox
Date      : Nov 10, 2009 at 5:19 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

Thanks for your support guys !

Today, I've started the domes. Well I did just one half, 3 more to build lol

Thanks to Scratchy (Jay) to helped me on that with his files (I did some modifications to them, gonna send them to you Jay). He had a great idea to build one half with only one piece of styrene. Easy and precise (well easy at studio scale, not easy at the scale he's doing his ISD :lol).

Here's the first result, took me 3 hours (needs to be sanded) :

[IMAGE: 8ft96.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft97.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft98.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft99.jpg]

I used very thin styrene (0.3mm), I will do some internal ribs to give it rigidity and the correct shape then I will pour resin once the 2 halves are glued together, it will be very strong. I also build a rotocasting machine today, this way I will be able to get hollow domes for weight purpose...

Click to expand...

 

Thanks Taz, I bought some months ago crystals but the faces are not perfectly done 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 The ones on your site looks better, unfortunatly they is not the size I need (2" diameter)

Jay, there are some misalignement (about 1/10 of millimeter but that's enough) between the triangle faces when I glue them. I cant do better 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Gonna try to get them 3D printed as this is the only way to get something perfect (because even with stock crystals, you're not sure you've got a 100 accurate dome because of the proportion of the triangles which can be slightly different from a manufacturer to another).

Thanks for your kind words though ! 

I finished the radar (it's missing some parts but I dont have pics good enough to ID them) then I primed it. There's also a pic with my hand to give an idea of the size : 

[IMAGE: 8ft112.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft113.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft114.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft115.jpg]

Post #193  (forum post #1071577)
Author    : MonsieurTox

Reactions : Like — struschie
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

Thank you Kevin !

Yesterday I received my kit which had the kind of radiators part on the left side of the neck. I cut them, unfortunatly (I knew that), my 3 styrene plates were 1 mm too high and the spacing between them was 1 mm instead of 0.5mm. Doesnt sound huge, but when you add them all, that's makes almost 5 mm... So I stripped off the plates and re did the plating job... My first plates were also too long but with new ref pics Ive been able to get them perfectly proportionned and scaled.

[IMAGE: 8ft121.jpg]

On the other side, I also glued the F1 radiator parts, here again my styrene plate was a bit too high. This time, I just cut a strip. 

[IMAGE: 8ft122.jpg]

I sprayed primer, that's quite hard because where I paint it's very cold, but I was able to get a decent result with the use of an hairdryer. 

[IMAGE: 8ft123.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft124.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft125.jpg]

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

I cant thank you enough for all your kind words guys... Im glad you like it !

I spent my night re drawing all my plans for the hull and building parts, now they are done, I just have to convert each part in .dxf now.

Today I built the assembly which goes on the very front of the superstructures. I had a very good pic of the non-hero side so it was easy to ID all the parts :

[IMAGE: 8ft149.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft150.jpg]

I cant say the same with the hero side... the only pic I have is this one, as you can see the resolution is poor... I found (I think) the main parts, but I cant find the fine details :

[IMAGE: 8ft153.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft152.jpg]

If someone has a good pic of the hero side of this assembly, I would love to see it, thanks !

And the top : 

[IMAGE: 8ft151.jpg]

Im missing a Yamato part (the vintage kit), I was wondering if someone could loan me this part that I can cast it ? (I used mine on the back of the neck, I didnt know it was used elsewhere).

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

Thank you for the support guys ! I appreciate it.

I built the small hangar :

[IMAGE: 8ft154.jpg]

Then I spray primer, I dont know if it's because of the cold weather but the gray tamiya primer is not as flat as it used to be, it looks like their white one now... I dont like the result because of the reflects it looks like the coat is heavy, fortunatly that's just an impression, should be nice once painted with the flat basecoat...

[IMAGE: 8ft155.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft156.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft157.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft158.jpg]

Yeah that's a nut. It is on the actual prop, actually the hangar ceiling sits on the armature tube and there is a bolt which goes through this tube. They had no other choice than drilling a hole in the ceiling. 

You can see in the pic on the right the bolt (topside) which goes through the tube : 

[IMAGE: 8ft159.jpg]

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

Thank you guys ! I'm glad you like the subject as I do !

I decided to start working on the main hangar bay. I had to recreate the supports for the I beams. While they were all scratchbuilt on the ILM model, I just built 10 masters because I ran out of half rods to make them : 

[IMAGE: 8ft160.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft161.jpg]

The first batch of parts (sorry for the color, I had to tweak it quite a bit because it was white resin on white plexi... not a good idea 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
) :

[IMAGE: 8ft162.jpg]

Took me 5 hours to align them and glue them all... That's not perfect but that's at least as good as the original model if not better :

[IMAGE: 8ft163.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft165.jpg]

Ive also built the rear bulkhead and started to detail it... Because of the lack of good ref, those are the only parts I was able to ID : 

[IMAGE: 8ft164.jpg]

Dry fit : 

[IMAGE: 8ft166.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft167.jpg]

The I-beam are on the way but I dont expect them before 2-3 weeks...

Thanks for looking !

Today Ive been working on the crane : 

[IMAGE: 8ft168.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft169.jpg]

It's not accurate to what it was for TESB, it was modified later. The pinches of the crane were symetrical (a bit like the ANH one) but it was modified at some point for ROTJ (I havent checked the movie yet) or, my best guess, for the reshot of the opening of ANH (IMAX version, they modified the TESB ISD to look like the ANH one, they even added some flaps on the engine bells).

Well I took some screengrab of TESB where we can see the hangar, unfortunatly there is no good close up. But I noticed something interesting, in one of the scene where the Star Destroyer is chasing the Falcon, the docking bay is unfinished... I mean there is no ribs on both side and the rear bulkhead is blank... no one kitparts ! In another shot, it's complete. That's not the first time the Destroyer was used while unfinished... In another shot the domes are not finished... No spindle, raised triangular panel etc...

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

I will never thank you enough for your kind words guys ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Rob : your're contributing more than with the pics ! Im following with great interest your awesome DS thread and Im taking note on how to do pencil lines ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Scratchy, modeleers, no I wont build any Blockade Runner in scale with the ISD... 

Stu, a fellow RPF member (I dont know if I can name him) contacted me a while back to help me for the plexi parts. I sent him the drawings, a few hours laters my parts were cut... I cant thank him enough for his help ! I'd receive the parts by the end of this week !

I have also good news about the domes, another fellow from the RPF did the domes for me. Because of me and of my poor explanations, they were a bit off, so he will redo them... Thanks to him too !!! 

If both of you dont mind, I would like to put your name as, I couldnt do what Im doing without your help guys !

Robert, big thanks for those pics ! Ive been able to ID some more parts, one of them is quite big and I was hunting it for a long time but I hadnt good pics of it ! 

Here it is : 

[IMAGE: 8ft186.jpg]

Ive also noticed with Rob and Bob's pics that I did a mistake when gluing the forward hangar door... The kit part was actually cut in half and a strip of styrene was added in the middle to enlarge it. And it's even more clear on the pic with Mike Fulmer building the hangar since this part is unpainted, we can clearly see the styrene strip in the middle : 

[IMAGE: 8ft187.jpg]

I'm missing some more bits because of the lack of reference of just because I cant find the right parts. I'll add them at a later stage if I ever find them, if I cant, Ill scratchbuilt them or put instead of them similar parts... From the same kits used on the hangar of course, I dont want to betray the ILM's work.

Some pics with a primer coat : 

[IMAGE: 8ft188.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft189.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft190.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft191.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft192.jpg]

Thanks for looking !

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

Yes bro Ive read that ! Could be a possibility but in my opinion it was just a matter of design ! They changed several while building her (there was no bay on the back of the neck, they removed the kitparts, cut a hole, put the bay -that's why that's why this is a poor fit :lol and when they did that, the ISD what at the same painting stage or even more painted -I mean they had started the weathering-).

Basically I know all the red parts (to be short Tamiya Gepard, flak38, Enterprise, Scharnhorst, Esci Demag, Rocco Leopard, Hasegawa Karl etc...) but I would like to know what are the parts behind them (they can be seen at certain angles), here how it looks initialy :

[IMAGE: ISDILMbuildingpic11.jpg]

And I know they are some parts between the "shelves" but I can figure what they are 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 One of them looks like the back of the Junyo or Taiho but I dont know how it's cut, where it starts and where it finishes... Most of the time I know there is something but I dont have clear view because of the angle or of the shadow (or of the flash which washes out the parts :cry).

Thanks Lee and Stu,

Yeah that's I could have bought a small car but yeah an ISD is way better ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

I havent had a lot of time, but I managed some free time to build the wooden armature : 

[IMAGE: 8ft219.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft220.jpg]

It's not 100% exact (my bulkheads are thicker than the original ones, I used 18 mm wood instead of 1/2 inch thick wood.

I also cut (the most difficult part so far) the neck to fit the superstructures. when I built the last stage of the superstructures, I glued it 5mm to backward so I had some difficulties with the neck... wont be 100% perfect as Im 5mm off, but Im still happy I havent damaged the neck while cutting it.

[IMAGE: 8ft221.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft222.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft223.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft224.jpg]

The neck is roughly cut, now I havent to sand the edges I cut to get a nice fit. And I'll glue it in place ! 

Ive also built the "boxes" on the starboard sides. 

Thanks for looking, Julien

Click to expand...

 

Yeah Allan, that's all relative... Actually the hero side and rear superstructures were easy to do in comparison of the front ones, that I still have to finish... Identify the parts of the sides and rear was very easy because I have good ref pics and TBH, that's always the same parts ! :lol 

Only a large part gave me trouble on the rear... It took me a whole night (yeah even when Im sleeping I try to ID part in my dreams and sometimes it works, like in this case lol) to find it. 

But for the front superstructures... that's a whole different thing. Each part is a fight because of the lack of good ref. I dont count the hour I was staring at blurry pics... sometimes I find a parts after several days... but there are still a lot of parts I cant find because I dont even know how they look !! I just know there's something. And being alone working on this one doesnt help. 

While I have something like 98-99% of the parts of the side and rear superstructures, I know I got only 90-95% or so of the parts of the front. At some point, I will have to fill the gaps...

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

In 2006 I scratched and kitbashed a 1/2.25 SS Star Destroyer, I used some kits that were used on the 1:1 8 footer (mainly 1/700 battleships), but I used 1/72 and 1/76 tanks instead of the 1/35 stuff... 

On the 8 footer there are suspension parts from a 1/76 sherman, I used the sherman (well M10 !) suspension part from a 1/72 Finemolds Tie Fighter which gave the exact size for the parts.

Same with the AMT DV's TIE Fighter wing panels used on the 8 footer, I used the wingstar from a Finemolds regular TIE Fighter (the wings from the original TIE fighter were made from a regular wingstar) and scratched the rest...

Here is some pics of my 41" Star Destroyer : 

[IMAGE: ISD240.jpg]

[IMAGE: ISD243.jpg]

[IMAGE: ISD247.jpg]

[IMAGE: ISD249.jpg]

[IMAGE: ISD253.jpg]

Post #407  (forum post #1216364)
Author    : MonsieurTox
Date      : May 10, 2010 at 8:40 AM
Reactions : Like — Supercruise, struschie
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer

Thanks Tim and Jase 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

The story about the domes could very long as it started in august, 2009. I will just make it short (I could make a whole post about that, but that wouldnt interest you) and say a big thanks to Jon would did the domes two times (the first ones were off because of me) and he was doing to do them a third time because we thought the second ones were lost in the mail. I finally received them almost 2 months later and what could I say ? They're perfect in shape, they're hollow (to save weight) and Job also did the pylon for me. I cant thank him enough for his patience as I was very anal about the shape and I did him redo the CG model several times.

I still have some bits to had to them but they're almost finished. I used the correct spindles (not the crappy brass rods they added when they restored her). Those spindles were not on the original model when they designed it and you can notice that the ISD doesnt have them on some TESB shots. There was only a styrene chip on one triangle and a tiny kit part on another. They added them later for TESB maybe to match the 3 footer ?

[IMAGE: 8ft238.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft239.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft240.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft241.jpg]

I wanted the shape as perfect as possible (the first ones were only off by not even 0.5 mm but it ruined the shape) as it's the sign of the vessel IMHO !

Thanks Jon !

Dan, I can assure that being off by 0.5mm they have totally another shape, I still have those domes so I can post pic if you're interested. This dome is a very complicated shape which doesnt allow any 'guess', it's possible to be off by a couple of millimeters but only for large things. My superstructures are 10mm too short, but it's not noticeable because it's 800 mm long... trying to fit the kitparts is another story ! :lol

Click to expand...

 

Hey John,

Wow thanks for the kind words ! I deeply appreciate them and I'm glad you have some much interest for this build !

I cant take full credit for this though, and that's why this place is so nice, I was helped in many way by several friends from all around the world... USA, Japan, Brazil, UK, New Zealand etc... 

I know this model is far from being finished, but I would like to thank those who helped so far. First Chrome, he helped me a lot when Ive starting to ID the beastie. Unfortunatly he never came back to the RPF and I hope he's good. BlackPig and Rick Deckard for the help to find several parts, DirtyDave, Stu, Faustus, BobaFlint for the Tamiya Shinano hulls, Allan H and Lee R for the T34 parts, Kbilly for the Shinano and Entex Porsche parts (that I still have to finish to mold !), Jon F and Jon K for the plexi parts and domes, Bar who sent me the scaled domes who served to draw the final design, Ease Owyeung for telling me the brand and ref of the paint used on the original model, Jason E for some cool refs, and of course all the great support I got from you guys, every time I post an update. That makes me going forward. I hope I haven forgotten nobody... Sorry if I did.

That's a lot of people involved in this model ! 

As for getting the model next week-end, it wont happen as I'm waiting to move to my new house to start building the hull ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 I will eventually cut the ribs and make the armature. The more I think about how to do the hull, the more I want to go another way that they did. Today there are great stuff available and I think I'm gonna use a layer of forex (3 mm thick, while holes to save weight) then skinned with a 1 mm plexi layer. This way it will be more rigid (the original hull tends to sag) and lighter. It will be a bit more expensive but I want it lasts. 

As for the support, Im planning to use the bottom mounting point, but I would like to have the side, top and rear mounting points, like the original, mainly because it would be easier to detail, scribe, paint and draw the pencil lines if I can put the hull in all those positions !

Anyway thank you again John, I hope I'll be able to show some cool progress very soon ! 

Julien

Click to expand...

Thank you very much Stu !

Those were just a few parts but the vintage Shinano hull is used everywhere on the model, and without your help guys, it wouldnt have been possible to find all the Shinano kits I needed.

Sure you could help me !! You could build the metal armature, cut the wooden ribs and making the metal stand, and maybe cut the skin of the hull ? Postage wouldnt be a problem from New Zealand ? :lol Hopefuly I'll get some help from a friend, because I dont have the skills to weld metal. Speacking of the hull, I have a plan to save some weight and get it more rigid. 

I'm planning to make a first layer of 3mm thick forex (gonna drill holes to reduce weight) and I gonna glue a skin of 1 mm plexi on it. This way it will be lighter, more rigid than a 4mm plexi plate, but it will have the hard outer surface of the plexi.

It will cost a bit more, but I dont want to end up with a 150Kg model. If I cant get it under 100Kg it would be great... Im not sure if it's possible though.

Ceric Neesh said:

			I don't think I would ever have the patience  or skill to even consider attempting anything of this magnitude.

Click to expand...

Thank you Ceric.

Hummm what to do with the left over parts ? I could build a Slave One, AT-AT, 32" Falcon, Snowspeeder, probe droid, med frigate... all the models they built with the left parts from the donor they used on the ISD ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 I dont know yet what will be my next project, I would love the Neb B but I'll have no room so probably a small model like the 32" Falcon or Snowspeeder. 

That's true that sometimes I used just a part from a kit, but for most of the kits, I used between 50 and 80% of the parts...

Post #474  (forum post #1275881)
Author    : Stormtrooper
Date      : Jun 30, 2010 at 12:47 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer (portside primered, lots of pics)

vaderdarth said:

			Wow man, that is the most respectable SS build I've ever witnessed.
		

Click to expand...

I absolutely agree... this is IMHO the pinnacle of Studio Scale Modelling. I've been waiting for these last pics with primer, for what seems like ages... makes a BIG improvment to the overall look of the model :thumbsup

vaderdarth said:

			You are going ten times faster than ILM and they had an entire crew working on this rig.....LOL
		

Click to expand...

 

IMO Julien's achievement is waaay more impressive than ILM's original build. Remember he's having to anaylse and examine hundreds of film stills and behind-the-scenes pics, to identify which parts were used for the original model, made over 30 years ago... then attempt to source the donor kits which were probably stacked to the ceiling in the local model shops of the day  :confused

They simply had to build a large spaceship that they could finish by adding kitbashed pieces onto it... if it looked 'right' then it went on.

Julien's having to ID each individual piece and then incorporate it into the model so that it looks like the original model from 1979. This requires a skill level far-and-beyond any skill that the ILM'ers had, if you ask me 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

These pics show the model to be super-clean and showing an already immensive sense of scale :thumbsup

Now, let's see some more pics, Julien... and no need to apologise! We're lovin' it!

Cheers,

John

Harish said:

			Greatest Studio Scale build of all times!!! The time, money and effort is astonishing! All original kits right? You're not using any castings????
		

Click to expand...

 

All original kits yes, some of the parts are castings though (there are 6 castings, now I have more original parts so I could replace them, but too much work lol), that's not bad considering I've glued more than 2500 parts so far. I will use more castings though, like the Entex parts because this kit is too expensive and I likely prefer to buy 100 Gneiseneau and King George V to complete this one to get thousand of parts than buying a single kit for 4 parts which are actually half pipes. :lol

Click to expand...

 

Thanks Eric, I think several SS models can be compared to the ISD... Some come to mind like the Death Star, the original ISD (less parts but the kits are probably harder to find !), the Battlestar Galactica, I guess the first one to work on one was a hero as it was probably the biggest SS model ever done by a casual modeler ! 

And of course your SandCrawler, you're the first one to make the crawler Eric, I would have love (and I hoped !) to be this first one, but I'm just glad you built it, so well. This one is really a tricky one because of all the angles, ANH donor kits that are always a ***** to find and not to mention that yoou made it R/C. Just making it R/C is probably the biggest challenge of this project, having something that actually runs, and runs well, is not easy but yours looks to run fine ! I'm so glad you didnt give up and you made it R/C.

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer (portside primered, lots of pics)

Even though I know now, from experience, that I'm going to be amazed every time I open this thread to find that Julien has posted new progress pics, without fail I come away even more impressed and inspired than I ever thought possible.

In fact, I will confess to staying up late on the occasional Friday or Saturday night, going back to the very first post in this thread and over in the corresponding parts ID thread, and reading through every message and ogling every photograph all over again. It's like some kind of studio scale porn...

The words "epic" and "awesome" are way overused today and have lost some of their meaning as a result. Even so I can think of no two words that more accurately describe what Julien is doing with this build, and the fact that so many people from our community have pitched in to identify parts and offer him support.

Epic.

Awesome.

After calculating the size in length I came up with 64' if you chose to do a Executor at this same scale. This is knowing that the Executor is 8X the length the regular ISD which is what you are building. So that being said and if you DO choose to go down that route which you do have my wish of God Speed to thee. Then Good luck and hope you do have the space for it. After all it will not be exactly the smallest model to ever be built.

Back on this current one I also give you my wish of God Speed to thee. Can't wait to see it finished and I am running out of things to say XD

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer (portside primered, lots of pics)

Thanks you guys to still showing interest in this model after all this time ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

John, I'm really sorry, I would love to have some update to show you, unfortunatly that won't happen for the 3 next months. 

Almost every kits is packed up for my move, getting a new job and the prep for the wedding (a second job 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
) keep me away from big projects and I just work on small models like the Shuttle or X-Wings. 

Then once I move to my new house, I have to setup my shop, right now I'm just tired to have to move the whole thing (it's so heavy and not enough space, I could break some parts) each I want to work on another area. Fortunatly in my new shop I will be able to turn around the model which will be easier and faster ! 

I also need to drawn again the plans for the hull as I lost them in my computer crash. 

Right now, I'm focused on the Shuttle which I want to be finished before the move (I don't know if it will be possible when I see how long the kits I've ordered are taking to arrive... probably because of christmas). 

If I can get the ISD finished for the 30th of ROTJ, that would be just great... And that would be my 30th anniversary too ! Only the end of the World in 2012 could stop me ! Or more probably a baby. :sleep

If you ever want to start with the 8 footer as a first SS model, why not ? 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 I would be glad to help ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 That's probably not the hardest model to do ! One of the biggest, most expensive, most time consuming, yes, but once you got your drawings right, the building is not very hard ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Post #578  (forum post #1469894)

Date      : Dec 8, 2010 at 10:59 AM
Reactions : Like — Supercruise, struschie
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer (portside primered, lots of pics)

Thank you guys !

I finally have an update for you, one of the top access hatch.

Once again I've tried to be as accurate as possible when scribing the lines and gluing the styrene chips, but it's hard to be 10% dead-on, some areas are not clear.

There're 223 (I like this number 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
) styrene chips and I take about 2 min to figure the location, lenght and width of a chip, cut it, sand it and glue it in place. Do the maths ! I don(t know how many styrene chips will be on the whole model ! (and I don't want to know :lol).

The first pic is to show I received my plates, I had to sand smooth the top and the edges. was easy and quick, the trickiest thing was to get sharpe wedges where they were rounded.

[IMAGE: 8ft309.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft310.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft311.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft312.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft313.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft314.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft315.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft316.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft317.jpg]

That's not a big update, but I hope you'll enjoy it.

Click to expand...

 

I built a wooden frame, trying to mimic the original : 

[IMAGE: 8ft219.jpg]

[IMAGE: tmakingoftesbISD.jpg]

Unfortunatly I didnt have the pic above when I built my frame, that's why mine isnt 100% accurate and it has 4 holes instead of 3.

With this frame , the whole thing is strong as hell, and the superstructures frame will be screwed to the hull frame (you can see in the pic of the original model that there are 4 wooden blocks, the screws go through them).

Today I built the master for the guns.

[IMAGE: 8ft318.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft319.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft320.jpg]

I need to fill some seams lines, but I'm happy with what I ended up.

Each guns is made of 5 parts, this parts, 2 guns supports and the 2 guns (which are kitparts, not castings).

Post #600  (forum post #1479955)
Author    : MonsieurTox
Date      : Dec 16, 2010 at 4:58 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer (portside primered, lots of pics)

Thank you guys, im glad you like !

Stu, this pattern is used at least 3 times (more kitparts added to the castings on the hero side). Each pattern is used more or less 3 times, and airbubbles dont like, those are castings ! They even used portion of y-wing castings ! Some portion of the trenches are 100% kitparts though. It's easy to see if thats a casting or not, the shelves of the castings are not flat but have an angle while the shelves of the portion detailled with kitparts are stock, flat, styrene strips. You know they even used castings on the 32" mf instead of real kitparts (im thinking to a gepard part used on the right mandible wall. They could have used an original kitpart but for some reason they didnt. This part casting is also used on the ISD superstructures.

For the trench castings, thats obvious they saved a lot of time, same apply to the turret !

Re: Building the 8' Star Destroyer (portside primered, lots of pics)

Hi Julien,

You could turn a master, and then make an inner and outer mold to ensure wall thickness is maintained.

Use a good quality rubber you could pick up all the detail on the master

High temp resistant resin is easily obtainable here in the UK to cast them.:thumbsup

Those were the last parts that you and Blackpig ID a few wweks ago

Thank you very much ! :$ Yes, I already put the FO in the bridge and have started to drill the holes on the front of the superstructures and on the hero side ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 Very time consuming... I gonna use warm white LED's though !

neosporing said:

			i'll pay money to see this!

Click to expand...

Uncle Lucas wont be happy if people pay to see the model ! :lol

You're welcome if you're going to France to visit me though ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

The tan disk if from the Bandai Schwimm.

I was missing the details on the top of the back of the neck, I scratched them but wasnt totally happy with them. Then our very BlackPig found THE part. After some reflexion,I thought I was ready to do the modifications... Of course you're always a bit nervous when you're trying to remove parts/assemblies off something like the ISD.

That's how it looked : 

[IMAGE: 8ft346.jpg]

Started to shave all the details : 

[IMAGE: 8ft347.jpg]

And now the awesome find of BlackPig... The barrels of the Nelson/Rodney still attached to the sprue ! Of course the sprue itself needs to be sliced in half... without breacking any of the barrel part ! Hehe, now that's some kind of sport 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

[IMAGE: 8ft348.jpg]

New turrets were added as I destroyed the old one when I removed them.

Masking :

[IMAGE: 8ft349.jpg]

And primered, of course, even if that's the same brand of primer, it's not exactly the same color... maybe because the neck was primered one year and a half ago too :

[IMAGE: 8ft350.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft351.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft352.jpg]

Thanks BP ! You rock !! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Click to expand...

 

Thanks Joe !

I think it's looking so good because the original is just awesome ! It's easy to come up with a great looking model when you're replicating this piece of History ! When you replicating it you realize they havent put the kitparts randomly, that's a very clever job (of course some parts were just here to fill a gap ! :lol).

I really want this build to be a tribute to the ILM team who worked on those (and this one in particular) models ! 

And I'm glad to see there are lately always more people recrating those awesome models... Rob's DS, Eric's sandcrawler, Lee's and Guy's PD, Phil's Falcon... etc there're too many to count ! All the are a great tribute of the guys who worked on the best FX models (I'm including the guys who worked on the Galactica models). Don't get me wrong I like what the CG guys are doing today, but TBH that will never bit the physical models ! 

ralphee said:

			Julien, thats a great find, and a great save.....or, great "shave" should i say :lol.

lee
		

Click to expand...

 

Thanks Lee ! 

Yeah I was a bit nervous about the surgery lol But I couldnt have passed on this ! 

Yeah the hue is different, the Tamiya one is a bit lighter, it's also a bit thicker and shiny. I think you're right that's because of the new laws about chemical formulas... We'll have to live with that now lol

Post #696  (forum post #1771151)
Author    : MonsieurTox
Date      : Jul 17, 2011 at 5:38 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thank you guys, appreciate your interest ! 

I have no secret data, I just use every pic I found over the year on the internet. Most of them were taken by rpf members (Frank Wire's and Martyn's (Nwerke) sets are very complete and pics are of great quality. However, due to the way she's displayed (in a large display case, it's hard to take good pics of several areas (glass reflects). Some times it's very hard to figure the shape of a part but with the help of BlackPig, everything is possible ! Pictures of the Chronicles and Sculpting a Galaxy books are also great references (unfortunatly there's not enough of them !). 

Detailling wise I think I'm way more than 40%, the brim trenches are not that detailled (only a few more kitparts on the resin castings), the most challenging part now (not counting making the inner frame and the main hull) will be ID'ing the parts if the engine areas. While most of them are easy to spot, several ones are hidden (or unknown from me). Still a lot of work to achieve, but to be honest, i would love this model to be an endless build... I enjoy each moment spent on it !

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thank you Mauiman. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

I ask again we never know... I'm still looking for the part they used for the leading edge. I opened a thread about it a while ago and was suggested it could be H beams or spacers. Unfortunatly I havent found something with the right size and shape.

Here's what I'm looking for : 

http://juliensmodelshop.com/leadingedgefinaldrawings.pdf

It's not symetrical (look at the cross section, just keep in mind I havent taken any measurements so the proportions are a bit of but you get the basic shape and how the whole leading edge was constructed).

They used regular brass channels on the SSD (and on the ANH ISD, see excellent Rick's building thread), and I have the feeling it's also brass or some kind of metal (at least for the part I'm looking for, the strips they added seems to be styrene, a lot of them are broken now and brass wouldnt break this way).

Any help would be much appreciated, thanks guys !

Thanks guys ! And sorry, that's true Ive been quiet those last few months.

The truth is those last few months Ive only been one day a week at home... And of course I've spent this day with my wife (when possible because my day off is not always the week-end). 

I spent this little free time making molds for the ISD (trenches), Y-Wing and I've started to mold my hero x-wing upper fuselage. The fuselage is still in rubber (for 3 weeks now lol I need to poor some plaster on it to get it rigid). 

I havent given up on the ISD though. I'm still trying to ID the missing parts ont he bridge (with no luck, I've just found a part), starting to ID the engine area (easy to ID a lot of parts but several ones remain unknown, I'm not even sure they are kit parts, I mean all the big curved pipes... I need your help !).

That's funny you post on my thread now cuz yesterday I finally bought the wood I need to start the hull frame. I bought a huggge plywood plate for this, I'm still refining my drawings but I should start to cut the ribs next week if I have some free time. Ive bought a saw that will allow me to easily get chamfreined edges. 

Yesterday I finally found some time to glue some parts together to make... the very front assembly of the hull ! 

[IMAGE: isdfrontassembly.jpg]

(sorry no pic I'm not at home).

I've also been very pleased to find the same plastruct lamps which were used on the Dispatch pods (fortunatly enough, I have some spares !).

[IMAGE: isdplastructlamp.jpg]

Another thing is that my wife and I are curreclty looking for a new house (closer to our jobs) and we're (I am 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
) looking for a house with a room for my shop. I think we found the right one. The house will need some work but hell, I'll be able to build my ISD in this room ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Thank you for your interest anyway, this project is far from being dead, I want a 8 footer, and I'll get one !

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Yeah that could be an idea ! I was thinking to paint her in my grandparent's garden, it's big enough it's big enough to get the paint diluted in the air to not bother the neighbors ! 

I'm planning to get her in 2 parts (there's a seam between two plates on the actual ILM model, that's where it will split in two !). I will get one 160 cm long part (the front) and one 90 cm long part (the rear, well actually the wide will become the lenght lol this part is about 130 cm wide lol). I should be able to put the parts in my car (of course it would requiere 2 trips but that's always cheaper than rent a truck). 

My next mission is to find a 70 mm (OD) steel pipe, I would love aluminium to save weight though. I'm not sure about a PVC pipe, it could sag over time, even with this diameter. I dont think I'll build the side mounting points so it should be easier to build.

If anyone here worked on the shape of the 8 footer hull, I would be interested ! (I would cross check with my drawings, I'm sure of the angle of the ribs -more or less 1°- but the angle of the hull panels are harder to get right).

I also have hard time to figure how deep are the brim trenches, I got a result very close to 2" (whithout the edge extensions) which is very appealing because it's a standard measurements, but I cant be really sure since I have no kitparts with me...

Click to expand...

I should have commented this earlier check out ponoko (3D printing, laser cutting, cnc milling) they call it a "making system". Allows you to upload 2d or 3d files an get them cut or grown free to join just have to pay for cut/grown time an material. I believe they have two locations in Europe (London an Paris) might be worth checking out.

Thank you very much for your kind words guys, I'm glad you like watching this build and I'm sorry I'm so low 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

But some updates !

Thanks to new Steven's ref pics of the ISD he posted here, I've been able to make the rear of the bridge more accurate 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Of course I had to scrap everything :wacko

[IMAGE: 8ft378.jpg]

I didnt know what I was doing and was a bit scared with the idea I could break something (and I did 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
, the T rods, cranes and spins of the domes are very fragile ^^)

Actually I did the plating around the kit parts, while they did the plating before adding the kitparts (except the StuG and Mobel parts that were glued first). So I removed everything, kitparts, plating etc and did new plating, much more accurate as I was missing a lot of the panel, actually the whole rear is plated 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

[IMAGE: 8ft379.jpg]

Kitparts :

[IMAGE: 8ft380.jpg]

I feel like I already did that some years ago... :lol

Other side :

[IMAGE: 8ft381.jpg]

Primed :

[IMAGE: 8ft382.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft383.jpg]

Of course I'm pretty sure you barely see the difference ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Now some details that were unseen in the previous ref pics !

[IMAGE: 8ft384.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft385.jpg]

Thanks for watching and for your interest after all these years ! =)

OK, here you go ! 

While I bought enough Sherman, I had to cast some suspension parts because I lost one full kit... Well it could have been worse, I bought them 3 years agoa nd they came in bag so they can easily be lost.

Im back at casting (I'm casting your last parts too guys, you know who you are 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
) ! And I'm casting better and better ! Now I can cast intricate parts without any problem :

[IMAGE: 8ft387_zps300b9435.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft388_zpsc1d786cc.jpg]

Well unfortunatly those little rods are very fragile and I broken most of them when manipulating the large assembly 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 Some of them are broken on the original so I wont cry for that.

That's 3 days of work (not counting the blueprint drawing time) :

[IMAGE: 8ft389_zps23b33e49.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft390_zpsf0c5d4f3.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft391_zps7f4add31.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft392_zpsdaa76619.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft393_zps84a051d8.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft394_zps67d99bee.jpg]

That's all for now !

I have some more parts to find, I will post them soon, we never know.

Thanks Lee !

Well I thought 3 days was a lot for that work. But I should admit i stared at ref pics sometimes for hourd to ID parts. I colored a lot of parts on pics to ask you guys if you had any idea about them, Ive never posted them yet because I found most of the parts after making the maps. Lol

Well those are good questions. When Ill be ready to start the hull ? First when Ill get the money to get it the plexi and wood parts cut, the steel armature welded.*

Then (and it's a bit your second question) I need to clean up my workshop and make some room for her. That's where im going to build her and where she will be displayed.

Ive got some cool info from Paul Huston like what kind of wood he used to build the inner frame. Those are precious info to get a strong frame !

[IMAGE: 8ft395_zpsa3b62283.jpg]

As you can all the rear of this wall is empty, I just cant see the parts used (I'm not even sure there are parts lol, there are not parts in the Chronicles pic but it's in progress... and I think they added a lot more parts for either ROTJ or Star Tour because a lot of part on the counter top parts are 1/20 DFV parts which are just poorly sprayed in white and you cant there's not black primer coat, the silver can be seen through).

You can notice the part ID'ed by Steve36uk, on this side the "plate" (well the wall actually

) is cut, just the round part is used. On the other side, they used the whole part.

Post #848  (forum post #2749642)
Author    : MonsieurTox
Date      : Feb 15, 2013 at 3:39 AM
Reactions : Like — Supercruise, struschie
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Ok some updates !

I built the conical engine bell masters for the secondary engines.

I built it myself to save some money but wasnt sure about the result... The first attempt was a disaster, it was way out of shape (couldnt get a perfect round shape lol).

So first I built this :

[IMAGE: 8ft402_zps926043fd.jpg]

Then wrapped it with 4 layers of 0.5mm styrene. The 2 inner layers are shorter to create a lip.

Eventually I ended up with that :

[IMAGE: 8ft405_zps7d8f052f.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft406_zpsbbaca0f7.jpg]

I was very happy ! Almost perfectly round (Im sure it's rounder than the original 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
), very strong and light.

Then I cut those 9 blocks. None of them are perfectly identical :

[IMAGE: 8ft403_zpsedd400c0.jpg]

On the round plate, with some greeblies :

[IMAGE: 8ft404_zps76934482.jpg]

Dry fit :

[IMAGE: 8ft407_zpsbf158292.jpg]

Now I had to built the inner tube. Of course I didnt had the right diameter (33mm and I wanted 35.6mm) so once again I layered some styrene around it ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

[IMAGE: 8ft408_zps5d9cc2bd.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft409_zpsb92154c3.jpg]

Everything glued in place, ready for primer !

[IMAGE: 8ft410_zps2e0742c4.jpg]

Light coat of primer (I had some air bubbles created at the edges of the lips, going to sand them).

[IMAGE: 8ft411_zps7e1cd892.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft412_zps375a9a42.jpg]

Almost ready to pour rubber on it !

I'm very proud of it, when I started this part I have very little hope to be successful but I think it is !

Click to expand...

Haha Joe, I would have love to be in the team if only I was born... 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

I've molded and pulled some engine bells and installed them on the boxes I previously built :

[IMAGE: 8ft413_zpsb527dc60.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft414_zps0169046d.jpg]

As you can notice they fit waaaaay better than the ILM ones, there's no the huge 2 mm gap all around the bell on the top box ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 Well to tell the truth I wanted to recreate this gap, however my cone is not narrow enough, it's a tad too wide where it meets the top box so it fill the entire cutout. Oh well it's noticeable where you're in front of them ! :facepalm

For the ones who followed this thread you may remember I built the master for the laser turrets. However I had one more part to build, the support of the guns.

[IMAGE: 8ft415_zpse4bc57b8.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft416_zps934cb24b.jpg]

I also molded the guns because I need a ton of them (16 for the turrets and plenty of them for all over the trenches). I have enough real kitparts for the turrets but I dont want to run out of them so I did a mold, I'm not sure I'm going to buy more of those PoW kits since I only need them to detail the trenches and the leading edges of the hull so I will probably cast all the parts I need.

[IMAGE: 8ft418_zps1c2aeb74.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft419_zps5728537d.jpg]

Well now the laser turret platforms... well at least the hero one ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 Took me 3 days to build it and it's not finished yet :

[IMAGE: 8ft420_zps80b00af4.jpg]

The small black platform took me 3 hours to cut, fit etc... I thought that would be very quick to do but no. 

[IMAGE: 8ft421_zpsb7a5a1a1.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft422_zpsc4abbc85.jpg]

I think most (if not all) of the lines of the platform were penciled, however I prefered to scribe the main lines. It will help to pencil the other lines.

Some news now...

I will show you the process of how I built a dome with one piece of styrene. Unfortunatly, it was not perfect so I will have to go with another way (3D printing ? Probably). 

[IMAGE: 8ft100.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft101.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft102.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft103.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft104.jpg]

Here some stuff which will detail the main hangar bay :

[IMAGE: 8ft105.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft106.jpg]

I've read somewhere that the kind of rails of the main hangar bay were from a loco kit. Actually those are every black pvc half round and H rods with half styrene disks. It can be seen on a pic of Fulmer building the hangar and it's easy to notice that those pieces are not evenly cut and glued (there are a ton to build, they could have cast the parts ! I will :$).

Ive also worked on the underside of the bridge which is almost done. I did some cool find !

[IMAGE: 8ft107.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft108.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft109.jpg]

[IMAGE: 8ft110.jpg]

I worked on the X array, it's also almost done, some minor details to add : 

[IMAGE: 8ft111.jpg]

Post #904  (forum post #3154531)

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Last TimeLord said:

			Amazing build! I'm sure you know this. I've really enjoyed this. thanks for sharing.
		

Click to expand...

Thank you TimeLord !

Master Tej said:

			Any recent developments on this?

- Master Tej -
		

Click to expand...

Yes ! In my mind. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 After a chat with Paul Huston it became obvious what they built is overkill, overheavy, and over oldschool ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 I really want something lighter for ease of move and transport, I think Im going to use Forex (Sintra for you US guys) for the large ribs, square tubing instead of round tubing? For the hull, I could use 3mm Forex with a lot of holes to save weight skinned with 1mm acrylic. 4mm acrylic would be way too heavy for that but I still need the outer coat to be acrylic (forex is to soft). I think I can save a lot of weight and it still will be as strong.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Julien I think this is a fantastic idea, I don't build much anymore but the SD was one project I thought long and hard about back in the day back on Rel's board.  Your idea for the skin with holes in it is fantastic and should keep the weight down too.  When I had the two footer laser cut I went with round holes in the ribs and regretted it.  I hope all is well and I know that some day I will be very green with envy over this.

Greg

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #908  (forum post #3154726)
Author    : Watson
Date      : Dec 29, 2013 at 10:53 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

MonsieurTox said:

			Hi Greg, good to hear from you !

Yeah I remember those good old days ! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Could you elaborate about the problems you had with the holes in the ribs ? I was planning to do some in mines. Did they have less rigidity ? I'm planning to use 15mm Sintra for them, should be plenty enough. I may add some plywood reinforcements here and there (mainly where the superstructures sit on the inner frame).
		

Click to expand...

Yeah I miss those days too 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

I was referring to round holes in the ribs where I ran the structural support rods through.  It made it difficult to line up the ribs .  Square holes with Square support rods will hold everything nice and true so they won't spin if you know what I mean.  Its just one less headache to worry about.

G

[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 I really want something lighter for ease of move and transport, I think Im going to use Forex (Sintra for you US guys) for the large ribs, square tubing instead of round tubing? For the hull, I could use 3mm Forex with a lot of holes to save weight skinned with 1mm acrylic. 4mm acrylic would be way too heavy for that but I still need the outer coat to be acrylic (forex is to soft). I think I can save a lot of weight and it still will be as strong.
		

Click to expand...

Sure. I mean it.

Hmmm, sarcasm or not, I don't feel Julien had to defend himself so nicely over a comment like this. 

Most just don't have a clue how long it takes to make a big SS replica model. A huge amount of time is spent pouring over ref continuously, building sections, re-doing & tinkering to get somewhat accurate.

Kit collecting can take years, Juliens SD is a major wallet depleter for sure. I spend around $5000 a year on kits for the Falcon as an example, that's around 4-5 years of collecting alone!.

We work on these alone, no around the clock crews, just one guy plugging away when time permits. 

Keeping up enthusisam for one build over say 3-8 years is tough too, but with the staggering amount of help & support from members here, it gets done, somehow!.

A positive comment goes a long way in fueling the fire for a big SS build!.

Stu

Post #934  (forum post #3348344)
Author    : Duncanator
Date      : Jun 25, 2014 at 10:59 PM
Reactions : Like — struschie
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I just finished reading through this entire thread and all I can say is "Wow!". Amazing work by you and all the folks who helped research the parts.

I wish we had your help when we repaired the real one back when it got damaged being shipped to the Smithsonian during the production of Episode 1. (or was it Ep 2? They kinda blur together.) At any rate, the reference we had was pathetic compared to what you guys have accumulated. And who knows how many repairs of repairs of repairs we were repairing. In addition to repairing the broken sections, we tried to replace as many lost parts as we could identify. I WISH we had your collective knowledge when we had to do that.

The damage to the big SD was pretty extensive. One of the large acrylic hull sheets had cracked and had to be replaced, and a number of parts had broken or fallen off including the conning tower which was completely smashed. I was tasked with rebuilding the conning tower from the pile of broken bits that the Smithsonian sent back to us. A funny thing was that; being the Smithsonian, all of the parts had been individually bagged in little ziplock bags including the dust, debris and broken fibre-optics strands that they swept out of the bottom of the crate. They were very thorough! I spent the next couple weeks matching up paint chips and glue marks in order to put the pieces back together. 

The "old guys" like Lorne Peterson and Steve Gawley could only remember things like "I think the ship kits were by Tamiya," so tracking down missing parts was a detective story for us, just like for you. You guys probably got more things right than we did due to our limited time. You all should be applauded for the research you've done to figure out what was used by guys who were just grabbing whatever looked good at the time. Truly amazing!
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #936  (forum post #3348712)
Author    : star-art
Date      : Jun 26, 2014 at 9:31 AM
Reactions : Like — struschie
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Wow! I noticed in some pics taken at the archive that the "nose" of the model was sagging. Was this from damage done during shipping as well? Looking at photos of it under construction, it seemed there might not be enough "structural integrity" to the armature to prevent this from happening. The hangar bay seriously cuts into the available space for structure in that part of the ship. (Funny thing is, the smaller 4-foot model had an even deeper hangar bay, so even less room inside the model.)

The reason I was studying this is because I am about to start building a 4-foot ANH version for a client. Engineering the structure has been a bit of a challenge. Julien, you might want to be very careful when designing the armature and bulkheads for your 8-footer. If the sagging nose was *not* the result of a shipping incident, it might indicate structural weakness in the design itself. 

Also, recently I was very lucky to have the opportunity to do some repair work on the original Battlestar Galactica filming model. After more than 35 years the glue bonds were starting to fail and the parts kept flaking off. We were very lucky to know where almost every single missing part went and we brought quite a few spares with us. I can only imagine though what might happen if that model were to be shipped somewhere. . .

Having built two studio-scale replicas of the Galactica and having shipped both of them successfully, I honestly can't believe how the studios transport these kinds of items. From what I can see, they build a wooden platform and mount the stand and model to it. Then, they assemble a wood crate around it. The trouble is, ALL shock and vibration is transmitted directly to the model this way. When I crate a model, I suspend it in a bed of very soft foam rubber inside the wooden structure. The idea is to make sure there is no direct contact between the crate and the ship. I know this requires a lot of effort and planning. But, if I was in charge of shipping something as priceless as a screen-used Star Destroyer, I would spare no expense or effort to make sure it got to its destination unscathed. WTH?
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #940  (forum post #3349106)
Author    : star-art
Date      : Jun 26, 2014 at 4:11 PM
Reactions : Like — asalaw
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I suspect it failed at the point where the tube ends. A 3-inch diameter tube is HUGE. I think that could be way overkill -- even for a model this size. I would probably use 1 1/2" IPS pipe. It's thicker and stronger than metal tube. A Schedule 40 pipe should work very well. The actual outside diameter is just 1.9 inches. You might be able to extend it almost all the way to the nose. Plus, you can use off-the-shelf fittings for the model mounts. PM for more info. I can point you to the ones I use in the Galactica.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #941  (forum post #3349335)
Author    : Duncanator
Date      : Jun 26, 2014 at 8:33 PM
Reactions : Like — struschie
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Most of the strength for the model comes from the aluminum tubes, so the nose that hangs off the end has very little support. You've got to remember, the mindset when building these models was that they only had to survive the shooting schedule. Most models of the day got thrown in the dumpster after the film was over. No one ever imagined that these models would still be around 35+ years later - or being shipped all over the world to be displayed. The plastics get brittle, glues start to let go and paint colors start to shift. Some of these old models just start raining parts when you move them around. They certainly weren't made to last decades after filming.

 The 4 foot X-Wing was another victim of that shipping event. Actually it was a victim of it's own design. Except for the central aluminum tube, the armature was made of acrylic and after 30 years it had gotten brittle. It came back looking like a model kit. Everything had dis-assembled itself: wings, engines, fuselage, lasers, cockpit… It looked like someone had clipped the parts off the sprues and tossed them back in the box.

  Lucasfilm uses a professional shipping company that is used to dealing with fine art; but with fragile things and thousands of miles, sometimes the worst happens.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #942  (forum post #3349338)
Author    : Duncanator

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

MonsieurTox

[URL said:
			
		

			http://i65.photobucket.com/albums/h203/monsieurtox/Divers/isdframe_zpsa91eccd9.jpg[/URL]

I agree with you, the hangar bay doesnt give that much room, the outer diameter of the tubing is 3" and that's a tight fit
		

Click to expand...

That may actually be a 2" ID aluminum tube. So the outside would be around 2 1/2" . A 2" mount rod was pretty common for the model mover mounts. We liked using 2" because it also matched the modular tubing rigging system that the grips used on stage.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #943  (forum post #3349409)
Author    : star-art
Date      : Jun 26, 2014 at 10:21 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I always wondered about this. Could it be that the '2" mount rod' was actually 1.9 OD? That is a very common IPS pipe size for things like railing. From what I understand, it was used for things like scaffolding and even lighting on stage. Many different fittings are available. This seems to match your description of a "modular tubing rigging system." 

 (A DP I know says they mostly use a smaller IPS pipe size but they sometimes use the bigger 1 1/2" IPS pipe that is 1.9 OD.)  

A 2.25" OD aluminum tube with a 1/8-inch wall thickness would be a loose slip fit over 1.9 OD pipe. But, it would *not* fit over 2-inch OD metal tube as that would be way too tight. You need a good 0.015" clearance all around the tube to get a telescoping fit -- 0.03" is even better. Using a 2.0 OD mount requires a thinner wall armature tube.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Those are the fittings for 1 1/2" IPS pipe. They are used to make railing, staging, scaffolding, etc. They are also used a lot in stage lighting, but I am told a smaller size is more common.

The PIPE that fits into these fittings is available from many sources. I use a special extruded aluminum that is "high strength" compared to regular pipe. This makes it a perfect choice when building armatures for large models. We can chat more when you get back. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Yup! Speed rail is the stuff the grips used on stage. The modelshop used thicker walled aluminum tube stock so that we could tap screws into it, but we kept the size compatible with the speed rail. Post #951  (forum post #3351424)
Author    : star-art
Date      : Jun 29, 2014 at 11:46 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I use roughly 1/8 inch wall pipe (~3mm) and that is extremely thick. I do believe you can get aluminum tube with a 1/4 inch wall, but that is WAY thick. I don't recall noticing in the pics it was that much?

He's saying the ID of the armature tube was 2 inches. The mount rod was also 2 inches, but it was machined down so it fit snugly inside the tube. 

If you simply try to use off-the-shelf parts, there is no way to get a telescoping fit with these materials. You can use 1 1/2" IPS pipe as your model mount and the fit will be a bit loose. You will need to shim the mount to get a tighter fit.

That's not much of an issue for me because I use IPS pipe both as the armature *and* as the model mount. Special adapters are available that give a tight friction fit and also a locking coupling when using the pipe.

As to shipping, no guarantees. It costs an arm and a leg to get that stuff shipped inside the States! They have a minimum order and a flat rate shipping fee. Not cheap. . .
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #953  (forum post #3352196)
Author    : Duncanator
Date      : Jun 30, 2014 at 8:48 AM
Reactions : Like — asalaw
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Haha! We have been throwing around a a lot of numbers!

The armature tube stock we used was 2 inches inside diameter. It had a 1/4" wall thickness that made the outside about 2.5 inches and was adequate for tapping screws into. Sometimes we would use a thinner walled tube and weld a small block onto it to add thickness where we needed to tap in a screw.

We would custom lathe mount rods to fit inside into this tubing with a "slip fit". We didn't want the fit too tight because it might bind or gall and become difficult to remove.

Speed rail; as Star-art mentioned, is used by stage crews for scaffolding, rigging etc… and it has an inside diameter of 1.5 inches and an outside diameter of about 1.9 inches.

Sometimes we would use the speed rail tubes to mount or move the models if the custom mount rod was too short or we needed extra mount points. The fit of the speed rail was a little loose, but it worked for emergencies.

I hope that clears it up.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #954  (forum post #3352202)
Author    : Duncanator
Date      : Jun 30, 2014 at 8:57 AM
Reactions : Like — asalaw
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

One other thing: If you are planning to weld your armature, make sure you get a weldable aluminum like 6061. 

High strength varieties of aluminum like 2024 or 7075 don't weld very well.

You may already know that from your ATAT project, but I thought I'd mention it.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #955  (forum post #3352269)
Author    : star-art
Date      : Jun 30, 2014 at 10:10 AM
Reactions : Like — asalaw
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

I had my first Galactica armature welded. It warped quite badly. This can be a problem with aluminum unless the person doing the welding is very experienced and knows exactly what he's doing. I've since switched to using bolt-together armature designs made with mostly off-the-shelf parts. It's a lot more cost effective -- and much easier to build.

Then again, there are times when a welded design is exactly what's needed. In that case, you might be better off using something like steel muffler pipe (what they used on the original Galactica).

One other point: Thick-walled aluminum tube can get quite heavy. Even the Sched. 40 pipe I use with a roughly 1/8 inch wall is heavy. With a large model like this, weight becomes an issue and needs to be kept under control. That's why I'd recommend something thinner than what was used on the studio model.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Duncanator said:

Click to expand...

Just caught up with this amazing thread!

Back when I was in the industry (80s and early 90s), speed rail was used for damn near everything unless regular scaffolding was called for. Sturdy and highly modular -- for example, the safety railing and other attachments on insert cars are speed rail so they can be quickly reconfigured for the needs of a particular shot. Also camera rigs on picture cars, for the doors and the hood, are usually MacGuyvered from speed rail with special suction-cup attachments (that's not what bears the load though). Given enough speed rail, bungee, and a high hat, those guys could rig a Panaflex to a blade of grass. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

It's easier to remember what I never saw it used for -- raising large lights outdoors. That was done with regular scaffolding. After a certain height, I assume a highboy becomes too top-heavy even if you bag the crap out of it (especially if you're raising an arc lamp), so they go to scaffolding and put the stand on top of that.

IIRC, the stuff I saw on set never varied from around a 2", maybe 2 1/2" diameter. I don't remember exactly (though I probably knew at some point, since I was always a gear geek). But it was always exactly the same everywhere I went, obviously because messing around trying to adapt different diameters from different rental houses could be a real time-suck on set.

Wow. Weird what you can suddenly remember after 25 years. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Here's a photo I found of a typical speed rail rig on a picture car:

[IMAGE: 180140-43c2e5c74ab7b89d388d0c3580906c50.jpg]

And here's a couple of insert cars, just swarming with speed rail:

[IMAGE: 180141-ba4d5cc35801ef06381252c36175896e.jpg]

[IMAGE: 180142-d0b6c4fb2272c7274c00a33c56be14cf.jpg]

[IMAGE: 180143-c8577a40abcaf2f38dc8c49c2c8e6c8d.jpg]

[IMAGE: 180144-ccb414a9558576de9326abc750f54efd.jpg]
